Causality and Created Things
beginner
4 min
Refuting the Philosophers' Claim That Temporal Huduth Requires Matter
Refutation of philosophers' claim that temporal huduth requires matter.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why temporal origination does not necessitate a material substrate, based on the argument from necessary-by-another and possibility.

Core Idea
Temporal origination does not need a material substrate; dependence on a cause suffices.

The philosophers argued that anything that comes into existence temporally must have a material foundation, either as a subject for accidents or prime matter for forms. The author refutes this by appealing to the established principle that the necessary by another must be possible, and its dependence is on its attribute of non-entitlement, not on a material substrate. This lesson examines that rebuttal.

Guided Path
1
Understand the philosophers' claim
Read the first part of the passage: the philosophers state that temporal huduth (being preceded by non-existence) requires a material substrate (madda), either a subject for accidents or prime matter for forms.
Note the distinction between accident and form.
2
Grasp the author's refutation
The author rejects the claim with 'laysa bi-shay' and explains why: the necessary by another must be possible because it depends on its attribute of non-entitlement, not on matter.
This connects to earlier discussions on necessity and possibility.
3
Connect to broader kalam principles
Reflect on how this argument fits into the larger debate about origination and the need for a creator. The refutation shows that temporal origination does not imply material composition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(وثانيها) أي ثاني أبحاث الحدوث (أنه قال الحكماء: الحدوث بمعنى المسبوقية بالعدم وهو الحدوث الزماني يستدعي مادة أي محلاً، إما موضوعاً إن كان الحادث عرضاً وإما هيولى إن كان الحادث صورةً، فليس بشيء؛ لأن الثابت فيما تقدم أن الواجب بالغير يلزم أن يكون ممكناً؛ لأنه موقوف على صفته التي هي اللا استحقاقية.
(And the second of them) i.e., the second investigation of origination (that the philosophers said: Huduth in the sense of being preceded by non-existence, which is temporal origination, requires a matter, i.e., a place, either a subject if the originated is an accident, or matter (hayula) if the originated is a form, so it is nothing; because what is established in what preceded is that the necessary by another must be possible, because it is dependent on its attribute which is non-entitlement.
Source pages p. 6

Commentary
This passage refutes the philosophers' claim that temporal huduth (being preceded by non-existence) necessarily requires a material substrate. The claim is that temporal origination demands a matter (madda) – either a subject (mawdu') if the originated is an accident, or hyle (hayula) if it is a form. The response is that this claim is baseless ('laysa bi-shay'), because what has been previously established is that the necessary by another (al-wajib bi-ghayr) is necessarily possible, since it depends on its attribute of non-entitlement (la-istiḥqaqiyya). That is, the dependence on a cause already accounts for its need, without requiring a material substrate. Thus, the philosophers' assertion is invalid.

Key Terms
حدوث
زماني
مادة
موضوع
هيولى
عرض
صورة
واجب بالغير
ممكن

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Temporal origination necessarily requires a material substrate.
Correction: Temporal origination does not necessitate a material substrate; the need for a cause is sufficient.

Checkpoint
Why does the author reject the philosophers' claim that temporal huduth requires matter?
A) Because temporal huduth does not involve precedence by non-existence.
B) Because the necessary by another is possible and depends only on its attribute of non-entitlement.
C) Because accidents do not need a subject.
D) Because temporal huduth applies only to God.

Key Takeaway
Temporal origination does not require a material substrate; the necessary-by-another's dependency is on its own attribute of non-entitlement, not on matter.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you reflect on your own existence, do you truly believe that you depend solely on Allah's will, or do you unconsciously assume you need some material support or inherent quality to exist? How would this shift in understanding affect your sense of reliance on Allah?
?
The passage shows that dependency does not require a physical substrate. Is there something in your life—a habit, a relationship, or a belief—that you have assumed must be grounded in a material or worldly foundation, when in reality it can be sustained directly by Allah? What would it mean for you to let go of that assumption and trust in His cause alone?

5 min
The Necessity of a Material Locus for Possibility
The commentator argues that possibility requires a material locus.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the possibility of a temporal being requires a material substrate that is eternal.

Core Idea
Possibility is a real quality that cannot float free; it needs a home in matter.

This lesson explores a foundational argument in Islamic metaphysics: that the possibility of a contingent thing cannot be an abstract concept but must inhere in a real substrate. The commentator establishes that possibility is an attribute of the possible thing itself, not of the agent, and therefore requires a locus. This locus, identified as matter, must be eternal to avoid an infinite regress.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to grasp the flow of the argument.
Notice the hypothetical question at the start.
2
Distinguish the two kinds of soundness (sihha)
Understand the distinction between the soundness pertaining to the possible thing (its possibility) and the soundness pertaining to the agent (its power). This distinction is crucial for the argument.
The two soundnesses are not identical.
3
Grasp why possibility needs a locus
The argument progresses: possibility is an attribute of the thing itself, cannot be separate from it, so it requires a substrate that is neither the thing nor separate from it.
4
Identify the conclusion
The conclusion is that the locus is matter (al-mada) and that matter must be eternal.
Otherwise, matter would need another matter ad infinitum.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نفسه المرصد الثالث - المقصد السادس : أبحاث الحدوث الممتنع . فإن سئل : لماذا كان الأمر كذلك، وأجيب بأن ذلك لكون الممكن في صحيح الوجود؛ دون الممتنع ، كان كلاماً مقبولاً. لولا أن الصحة العائدة إلى ذات المقدور وهي الإمكان مغايرة للصحة العائدة إلى القادر لكان هذا تعليلاً للشيء بنفسه، (متأخرة عنه ) لتأخر المعلول عن علته . وأيضاً إمكان الشيء صفة له نفسه، لا بالقياس إلى الفاعل وصحة الاقتدار عليه مقيسة إلى الفاعل، فلا يكون الآخر، وإذ قد ثبت أن لإمكانه محلاً ليس نفسه ولا أمراً منفصلاً عنه فهو (أي ذلك المحل أمر) متصل به أي بالحادث اتصالاً تاماً حتى يصح قيام إمكانه به وهو المادة ولا بد أن تكون قديمة عندهم. وإلا احتاجت إلى مادة أخرى وفي المباحث المشرقية إن ذلك الحادث تارة يوجد عن تلك المادة كالأعراض، وتارة يوجد فيها كالصور وتارة يوجد معها كالنفوس الناطقة . (فإن قيل) قوله : (لا بالقياس إلى (الفاعل وإن كان صفة له بالقياس إلى الوجود والعدم . قوله: (وهو المادة فيه أنه إنما يتم إذا لم يجز حدوث صفة المجرد أو حدوث جوهر مجرد في جوهر مجرد مع أنهم بنوا عدم جوازه على أن كل حادث مسبوق بمادة . قوله : ( ولا بد أن تكون قديمة بنفسها، أو باعتبار جزئها إن فسر المادة بالمعنى الأعم . قوله : ( وفي المباحث المشرقية بيان للاتصال التام الموجب لجواز قيام إمكان الحادث بالمحل . قوله : ( يوجد عن تلك المادة بأن يكون متقوماً بها، فيكون وجوده في نفسه هو وجوده فيها، فإمكانه هو إمكانه فيه فإن مآل قولنا : البياض يمكن أن يوجد في الجسم، وقولنا : الجسم يمكن أن يوجد فيه البياض واحد . قوله : ( وتارة يوجد فيها وإن لم يكن متقوماً بها، لكنه حال فيها محتاج إليها، فمآل وجوده في نفسه هو وجوده في المحل، فكذا إمكاناهما . قوله : ( وهو المادة فيه بحث لأنا لا نسلم أن المتعلق بالحادث منحصر في المادة بالمعنى المذكور، لم لا يجوز أن يكون محل إمكان الحادث شيئاً له تعلق بالحوادث وراء تعلق الحلول أو التدبير والتصرف، ولو كان تعلق الحلول فلم لا يجوز أن يكون الحادث جوهراً غير جسماني حالاً في جوهر آخر كذلك، ولم يقم دليل على امتناع ذلك، وأيضاً قد نبهت على أن الموضوع قد يكون جوهراً غير جسماني، كعلوم العقول، فيبطل حينئذ ما فرعوا على هذه القاعدة من قدم کمالات العقول ؛ لاستلزام حدوثها سبق المادة . قوله : ( وفي المباحث المشرقية تقوية لما سبق من تعميم المادة. قوله : ( يوجد عن تلك المادة كالأعراض المراد بالمادة المحل لا الهيولى، وإلا فالحركة الأينية والوضعية مثلاً لا توجد من الهيولى، بل من الجسم.
The third observatory - the sixth objective: investigations of temporal origination. The impossible. For if it is asked: why was the matter so, and it is answered that it is because the possible is in sound existence without the impossible, it would be acceptable speech. Were it not that the soundness (al-sihha) pertaining to the essence of the predestined (al-maqdur), which is possibility (al-imkan), is different from the soundness pertaining to the agent (al-qadir), this would be an explanation of the thing by itself, (posterior to it) because the effect is posterior to its cause. Also, the possibility of a thing is an attribute of itself, not in relation to the agent, and the soundness of being able to do it is related to the agent, so they are not the same. And since it has been established that its possibility has a locus (mahall) that is not itself nor something separate from it, so that locus is something (connected to it, i.e., to the temporal being) with a complete connection such that its possibility can subsist in it, and it is matter (al-mada). And it must be eternal (qadima) according to them. Otherwise it would need another matter. And in al-Mabahith al-Mashriqiyya, that temporal being sometimes emanates from that matter like accidents, sometimes exists in it like forms, and sometimes exists with it like rational souls. (For it is said: ) His saying: (not in relation to the agent) even if it is an attribute for him in relation to existence and non-existence. His saying: (and it is matter) contains that it is only completed if the occurrence of an attribute of a simple being or the occurrence of a simple substance in a simple substance is not permitted, given that they based its impermissibility on that every temporal being is preceded by matter. His saying: (and it must be eternal by itself, or by consideration of its part if matter is interpreted in the general sense). His saying: (and in al-Mabahith al-Mashriqiyya is an explanation of the complete connection that necessitates the permissibility of the subsistence of the possibility of the temporal being in the locus). His saying: (it emanates from that matter) by being constituted by it, so its existence in itself is its existence in it, so its possibility is its possibility in it, for the implication of our saying: whiteness can exist in the body, and our saying: the body can have whiteness in it is one. His saying: (and sometimes exists in it) even if it is not constituted by it, but it is inherent in it, needing it, so the implication of its existence in itself is its existence in the locus, so similarly the two possibilities. His saying: (and it is matter) contains a discussion because we do not concede that what is related to the temporal being is limited to matter in the mentioned sense; why is it not permissible that the locus of the possibility of the temporal being is something that has a relation to temporal beings beyond the relation of inherence or administration and disposal? And if it is the relation of inherence, why is it not permissible that the temporal being is a non-corporeal substance inhering in another substance likewise? And no proof has been established for the impossibility of that. Also, I have pointed out that the subject may be a non-corporeal substance, like the sciences of the intellects, so what they have built upon this rule concerning the eternity of the perfections of the intellects becomes invalid, because their temporal origination necessitates the priority of matter. His saying: (and in al-Mabahith al-Mashriqiyya is a strengthening of what preceded concerning the generalization of matter.) His saying: (it emanates from that matter like accidents) means by matter the locus (mahall), not the hyle (hayula), otherwise local and positional motion, for example, do not emanate from hyle, but from the body.
Source pages p. 10

Commentary
This is a continuous passage from the commentary establishing the necessity of a material substrate for the possibility of temporal beings. The passage first presents a hypothetical question about the possible and impossible, then refines the argument: possibility (imkan) is an attribute of the possible thing itself, not of the agent's power. Since possibility must have a locus, that locus is identified as matter (mada), which must be eternal according to the philosophers. The passage also cites al-Mabahith al-Mashriqiyya to illustrate three ways a temporal being relates to matter: emanating from it (like accidents), existing in it (like forms), or existing with it (like rational souls). The subsequent commentary (qawluhu) clarifies each part of the base text, including the distinction between the two 'soundnesses' (sihha), the nature of the locus, and a discussion on whether matter must be understood strictly as hyle or more broadly as any locus. The commentator also addresses an objection that the locus could be something other than matter, such as a non-corporeal substance, but notes that this would undermine certain arguments for the eternity of intellects. Overall, the passage argues for a real, external locus for possibility, foundational for proofs of the world's createdness.

Key Terms
imkan (possibility)
mahall (locus)
mada (matter)
qadim (eternal)
hadith (temporal being)
qudra (power)
sihha (soundness)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Possibility is merely a mental concept or a relation of the agent's power.
Correction: The passage argues that possibility is a real attribute of the possible thing itself, requiring an external substrate (matter). It is not just a mental concept nor a relation to the agent.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does the possibility of a temporal being require a locus?
A) Because possibility is an attribute of the agent's power
B) Because possibility is a real quality that cannot subsist without a substrate
C) Because matter is eternal
D) Because the possible and impossible are distinct

Key Takeaway
Possibility is a real attribute that inheres in a material substrate, which must be eternal.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You know now that possibility is not just a mental idea but a real attribute that needs a foundation. Have you ever considered that your own existence, with all its possibilities, is likewise not self-sufficient? What would it mean to live with the constant awareness that you are not your own ground?
?
The passage distinguishes between what a thing is in itself (its possibility) and its relation to an agent (power). In your daily life, do you confuse your intrinsic worth or identity with what you can do or achieve? How might this distinction change how you see yourself outside of your accomplishments?
?
If matter must be eternal to avoid infinite regress, then the chain of dependency ends in something that does not depend. Are you living as though you are merely part of an endless chain of causes, or have you anchored your hope in the One who is the end of all dependency? This lesson points to a necessary foundation—what is your ultimate foundation?

Causality and Created Things

Three Ways Temporal Beings Relate to Matter
The commentator presents a threefold classification of temporal beings' relation to matter.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three classifications of temporal beings in relation to matter as explained in al-Mabahith al-Mashriqiyya.

Core Idea
Temporal beings either emanate from matter, exist in matter, or coexist with matter.

After establishing that possibility requires matter, the commentator cites a key work, al-Mabahith al-Mashriqiyya, to illustrate how temporal beings are connected to matter. This lesson presents three categories: some emanate from matter like accidents, some exist in matter like forms, and some coexist with matter like rational souls.

Guided Path
1
Read the three categories
Read the Arabic passage that lists the three ways temporal beings relate to matter. Identify each category.
2
Understand the examples
Note the examples: accidents emanate from matter, forms exist in matter, rational souls coexist with matter.
3
Examine the commentary
The commentary explains each category in more detail. 'Emanation' means being constituted by matter; 'existence in' means being inherent and needing matter; 'coexistence' means existing alongside matter.
4
Reflect on the overall purpose
This classification shows the dependence of temporal beings on matter, supporting the argument that possibility requires a material locus.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نفسه المرصد الثالث - المقصد السادس : أبحاث الحدوث الممتنع . فإن سئل : لماذا كان الأمر كذلك، وأجيب بأن ذلك لكون الممكن في صحيح الوجود؛ دون الممتنع ، كان كلاماً مقبولاً. لولا أن الصحة العائدة إلى ذات المقدور وهي الإمكان مغايرة للصحة العائدة إلى القادر لكان هذا تعليلاً للشيء بنفسه، (متأخرة عنه ) لتأخر المعلول عن علته . وأيضاً إمكان الشيء صفة له نفسه، لا بالقياس إلى الفاعل وصحة الاقتدار عليه مقيسة إلى الفاعل، فلا يكون الآخر، وإذ قد ثبت أن لإمكانه محلاً ليس نفسه ولا أمراً منفصلاً عنه فهو (أي ذلك المحل أمر) متصل به أي بالحادث اتصالاً تاماً حتى يصح قيام إمكانه به وهو المادة ولا بد أن تكون قديمة عندهم. وإلا احتاجت إلى مادة أخرى وفي المباحث المشرقية إن ذلك الحادث تارة يوجد عن تلك المادة كالأعراض، وتارة يوجد فيها كالصور وتارة يوجد معها كالنفوس الناطقة . (فإن قيل) قوله : (لا بالقياس إلى (الفاعل وإن كان صفة له بالقياس إلى الوجود والعدم . قوله: (وهو المادة فيه أنه إنما يتم إذا لم يجز حدوث صفة المجرد أو حدوث جوهر مجرد في جوهر مجرد مع أنهم بنوا عدم جوازه على أن كل حادث مسبوق بمادة . قوله : ( ولا بد أن تكون قديمة بنفسها، أو باعتبار جزئها إن فسر المادة بالمعنى الأعم . قوله : ( وفي المباحث المشرقية بيان للاتصال التام الموجب لجواز قيام إمكان الحادث بالمحل . قوله : ( يوجد عن تلك المادة بأن يكون متقوماً بها، فيكون وجوده في نفسه هو وجوده فيها، فإمكانه هو إمكانه فيه فإن مآل قولنا : البياض يمكن أن يوجد في الجسم، وقولنا : الجسم يمكن أن يوجد فيه البياض واحد . قوله : ( وتارة يوجد فيها وإن لم يكن متقوماً بها، لكنه حال فيها محتاج إليها، فمآل وجوده في نفسه هو وجوده في المحل، فكذا إمكاناهما . قوله : ( وهو المادة فيه بحث لأنا لا نسلم أن المتعلق بالحادث منحصر في المادة بالمعنى المذكور، لم لا يجوز أن يكون محل إمكان الحادث شيئاً له تعلق بالحوادث وراء تعلق الحلول أو التدبير والتصرف، ولو كان تعلق الحلول فلم لا يجوز أن يكون الحادث جوهراً غير جسماني حالاً في جوهر آخر كذلك، ولم يقم دليل على امتناع ذلك، وأيضاً قد نبهت على أن الموضوع قد يكون جوهراً غير جسماني، كعلوم العقول، فيبطل حينئذ ما فرعوا على هذه القاعدة من قدم کمالات العقول ؛ لاستلزام حدوثها سبق المادة . قوله : ( وفي المباحث المشرقية تقوية لما سبق من تعميم المادة. قوله : ( يوجد عن تلك المادة كالأعراض المراد بالمادة المحل لا الهيولى، وإلا فالحركة الأينية والوضعية مثلاً لا توجد من الهيولى، بل من الجسم.

For if it is asked: why was the matter so, and it is answered that it is because the possible is in sound existence without the impossible, it would be acceptable speech. (For it is said: ) His saying: (not in relation to the agent) even if it is an attribute for him in relation to existence and non-existence. His saying: (and it is matter) contains that it is only completed if the occurrence of an attribute of a simple being or the occurrence of a simple substance in a simple substance is not permitted, given that they based its impermissibility on that every temporal being is preceded by matter. His saying: (and it must be eternal by itself, or by consideration of its part if matter is interpreted in the general sense). And no proof has been established for the impossibility of that. Commentary
This is a continuous passage from the commentary establishing the necessity of a material substrate for the possibility of temporal beings. The passage first presents a hypothetical question about the possible and impossible, then refines the argument: possibility (imkan) is an attribute of the possible thing itself, not of the agent's power. Since possibility must have a locus, that locus is identified as matter (mada), which must be eternal according to the philosophers. The passage also cites al-Mabahith al-Mashriqiyya to illustrate three ways a temporal being relates to matter: emanating from it (like accidents), existing in it (like forms), or existing with it (like rational souls). The subsequent commentary (qawluhu) clarifies each part of the base text, including the distinction between the two 'soundnesses' (sihha), the nature of the locus, and a discussion on whether matter must be understood strictly as hyle or more broadly as any locus. The commentator also addresses an objection that the locus could be something other than matter, such as a non-corporeal substance, but notes that this would undermine certain arguments for the eternity of intellects. Overall, the passage argues for a real, external locus for possibility, foundational for proofs of the world's createdness.

Key Terms
mada (matter)
a'rad (accidents)
suwar (forms)
nufus natiqa (rational souls)
hayula (hyle)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All temporal beings are made of matter or are material.
Correction: The passage shows that rational souls, though temporal, coexist with matter but are not themselves material. They are non-corporeal substances existing alongside matter.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which category do rational souls fall into?
A) Emanating from matter
B) Existing in matter
C) Existing with matter
D) They are not temporal

Key Takeaway
Temporal beings relate to matter in three distinct ways: emanation, inherence, or coexistence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider your own existence, do you see yourself as merely an accident of matter, or as a rational soul that coexists with matter? How does that shape your understanding of your purpose?
?
If your rational soul coexists with matter but is not material, what does that mean for how you treat your body? Do you live as if your soul is independent, or do you let bodily desires dominate?
?
In what ways do you experience the three categories in your daily life? Identify one thing that emanates from matter (an accident), one that exists in matter (a form), and one that exists with matter (your soul). How does this awareness change your perspective?

Objections to Matter as the Sole Locus of Possibility
The commentator discusses an objection that the locus of possibility could be a non-corporeal substance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the objection that the locus of possibility could be a non-corporeal substance, and why this view challenges certain arguments.

Core Idea
The substrate of possibility might not be matter but a non-material substance, undermining proofs for the eternity of intellects.

The opponent raises a critical objection: why must the locus of possibility be matter? Could it not be a non-corporeal substance, like the intellects? This lesson addresses that challenge and explains its implications for other philosophical arguments, such as the eternity of the perfections of the intellects.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
Read the passage beginning with 'قوله: (وهو المادة فيه بحث' which contains the objection. Notice the challenge that the locus is not necessarily matter.
2
Understand the alternative suggestion
The objector suggests that the locus could be a non-corporeal substance, such as the intellects, which are not matter.
3
Grasp the implications
If the locus can be non-corporeal, then the argument that every temporal being requires matter fails. This undermines the proof for the eternity of the perfections of the intellects.
4
Note the commentator's response
The commentator strengthens the generalization of matter but the objection remains open, as he acknowledges that the subject could be a non-corporeal substance like the sciences of the intellects.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نفسه المرصد الثالث - المقصد السادس : أبحاث الحدوث الممتنع . فإن سئل : لماذا كان الأمر كذلك، وأجيب بأن ذلك لكون الممكن في صحيح الوجود؛ دون الممتنع ، كان كلاماً مقبولاً. لولا أن الصحة العائدة إلى ذات المقدور وهي الإمكان مغايرة للصحة العائدة إلى القادر لكان هذا تعليلاً للشيء بنفسه، (متأخرة عنه ) لتأخر المعلول عن علته . وأيضاً إمكان الشيء صفة له نفسه، لا بالقياس إلى الفاعل وصحة الاقتدار عليه مقيسة إلى الفاعل، فلا يكون الآخر، وإذ قد ثبت أن لإمكانه محلاً ليس نفسه ولا أمراً منفصلاً عنه فهو (أي ذلك المحل أمر) متصل به أي بالحادث اتصالاً تاماً حتى يصح قيام إمكانه به وهو المادة ولا بد أن تكون قديمة عندهم. وإلا احتاجت إلى مادة أخرى وفي المباحث المشرقية إن ذلك الحادث تارة يوجد عن تلك المادة كالأعراض، وتارة يوجد فيها كالصور وتارة يوجد معها كالنفوس الناطقة . (فإن قيل) قوله : (لا بالقياس إلى (الفاعل وإن كان صفة له بالقياس إلى الوجود والعدم . قوله: (وهو المادة فيه أنه إنما يتم إذا لم يجز حدوث صفة المجرد أو حدوث جوهر مجرد في جوهر مجرد مع أنهم بنوا عدم جوازه على أن كل حادث مسبوق بمادة . قوله : ( ولا بد أن تكون قديمة بنفسها، أو باعتبار جزئها إن فسر المادة بالمعنى الأعم . قوله : ( وفي المباحث المشرقية بيان للاتصال التام الموجب لجواز قيام إمكان الحادث بالمحل . قوله : ( يوجد عن تلك المادة بأن يكون متقوماً بها، فيكون وجوده في نفسه هو وجوده فيها، فإمكانه هو إمكانه فيه فإن مآل قولنا : البياض يمكن أن يوجد في الجسم، وقولنا : الجسم يمكن أن يوجد فيه البياض واحد . قوله : ( وتارة يوجد فيها وإن لم يكن متقوماً بها، لكنه حال فيها محتاج إليها، فمآل وجوده في نفسه هو وجوده في المحل، فكذا إمكاناهما . قوله : ( وهو المادة فيه بحث لأنا لا نسلم أن المتعلق بالحادث منحصر في المادة بالمعنى المذكور، لم لا يجوز أن يكون محل إمكان الحادث شيئاً له تعلق بالحوادث وراء تعلق الحلول أو التدبير والتصرف، ولو كان تعلق الحلول فلم لا يجوز أن يكون الحادث جوهراً غير جسماني حالاً في جوهر آخر كذلك، ولم يقم دليل على امتناع ذلك، وأيضاً قد نبهت على أن الموضوع قد يكون جوهراً غير جسماني، كعلوم العقول، فيبطل حينئذ ما فرعوا على هذه القاعدة من قدم کمالات العقول ؛ لاستلزام حدوثها سبق المادة . قوله : ( وفي المباحث المشرقية تقوية لما سبق من تعميم المادة. قوله : ( يوجد عن تلك المادة كالأعراض المراد بالمادة المحل لا الهيولى، وإلا فالحركة الأينية والوضعية مثلاً لا توجد من الهيولى، بل من الجسم.
The third observatory - the sixth objective: investigations of temporal origination. The impossible. For if it is asked: why was the matter so, and it is answered that it is because the possible is in sound existence without the impossible, it would be acceptable speech. Were it not that the soundness (al-sihha) pertaining to the essence of the predestined (al-maqdur), which is possibility (al-imkan), is different from the soundness pertaining to the agent (al-qadir), this would be an explanation of the thing by itself, (posterior to it) because the effect is posterior to its cause. Also, the possibility of a thing is an attribute of itself, not in relation to the agent, and the soundness of being able to do it is related to the agent, so they are not the same. And since it has been established that its possibility has a locus (mahall) that is not itself nor something separate from it, so that locus is something (connected to it, i.e., to the temporal being) with a complete connection such that its possibility can subsist in it, and it is matter (al-mada). And it must be eternal (qadima) according to them. Otherwise it would need another matter. And in al-Mabahith al-Mashriqiyya, that temporal being sometimes emanates from that matter like accidents, sometimes exists in it like forms, and sometimes exists with it like rational souls. (For it is said: ) His saying: (not in relation to the agent) even if it is an attribute for him in relation to existence and non-existence. His saying: (and it is matter) contains that it is only completed if the occurrence of an attribute of a simple being or the occurrence of a simple substance in a simple substance is not permitted, given that they based its impermissibility on that every temporal being is preceded by matter. His saying: (and it must be eternal by itself, or by consideration of its part if matter is interpreted in the general sense). His saying: (and in al-Mabahith al-Mashriqiyya is an explanation of the complete connection that necessitates the permissibility of the subsistence of the possibility of the temporal being in the locus). His saying: (it emanates from that matter) by being constituted by it, so its existence in itself is its existence in it, so its possibility is its possibility in it, for the implication of our saying: whiteness can exist in the body, and our saying: the body can have whiteness in it is one. His saying: (and sometimes exists in it) even if it is not constituted by it, but it is inherent in it, needing it, so the implication of its existence in itself is its existence in the locus, so similarly the two possibilities. His saying: (and it is matter) contains a discussion because we do not concede that what is related to the temporal being is limited to matter in the mentioned sense; why is it not permissible that the locus of the possibility of the temporal being is something that has a relation to temporal beings beyond the relation of inherence or administration and disposal? And if it is the relation of inherence, why is it not permissible that the temporal being is a non-corporeal substance inhering in another substance likewise? And no proof has been established for the impossibility of that. Also, I have pointed out that the subject may be a non-corporeal substance, like the sciences of the intellects, so what they have built upon this rule concerning the eternity of the perfections of the intellects becomes invalid, because their temporal origination necessitates the priority of matter. His saying: (and in al-Mabahith al-Mashriqiyya is a strengthening of what preceded concerning the generalization of matter.) His saying: (it emanates from that matter like accidents) means by matter the locus (mahall), not the hyle (hayula), otherwise local and positional motion, for example, do not emanate from hyle, but from the body.
Source pages p. 10

Commentary
This is a continuous passage from the commentary establishing the necessity of a material substrate for the possibility of temporal beings. The passage first presents a hypothetical question about the possible and impossible, then refines the argument: possibility (imkan) is an attribute of the possible thing itself, not of the agent's power. Since possibility must have a locus, that locus is identified as matter (mada), which must be eternal according to the philosophers. The passage also cites al-Mabahith al-Mashriqiyya to illustrate three ways a temporal being relates to matter: emanating from it (like accidents), existing in it (like forms), or existing with it (like rational souls). The subsequent commentary (qawluhu) clarifies each part of the base text, including the distinction between the two 'soundnesses' (sihha), the nature of the locus, and a discussion on whether matter must be understood strictly as hyle or more broadly as any locus. The commentator also addresses an objection that the locus could be something other than matter, such as a non-corporeal substance, but notes that this would undermine certain arguments for the eternity of intellects. Overall, the passage argues for a real, external locus for possibility, foundational for proofs of the world's createdness.

Key Terms
mahall (locus)
jawhar mujarrad (simple substance)
uqul (intellects)
kamalat (perfections)
hayula (hyle)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The only possible substrate for possibility is material substance (hyle).
Correction: The objection shows that the substrate could be a non-corporeal substance, such as the intellects, which are not material.

Checkpoint
According to the objection, what would happen to the argument for the eternity of the perfections of the intellects if the locus could be non-corporeal?
A) It would be strengthened
B) It would become invalid
C) It would remain unaffected
D) It would require matter

Key Takeaway
The identification of the locus of possibility with matter is contested, with implications for arguments about the eternity of intellects.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You rely on your intellect daily. Have you ever considered that its substrate might not be material? How does the possibility that your thoughts inhere in a non-corporeal substance affect your understanding of your own soul? Will you ponder this today?
?
The objector claims that no proof has been established for the impossibility of a non-corporeal locus. Is there an area in your faith where you have accepted a theological claim without demanding proof? Could your certainty be built on assumption rather than evidence? Commit to examining one such claim this week.
?
If the perfections of the intellects are not necessarily eternal, what does that imply about the permanence of your own knowledge and achievements? Are you holding onto something as if it will last forever, while it may be temporal? Are you willing to trust in what is truly eternal—Allah alone—and detach from fleeting intellectual pride?

The Thesis on Contingents and the Perfection of the Necessary
States the two modes of emanation for contingents from the Necessary.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the emanation of a contingent being from the Necessary Being is either eternal (if its essential possibility suffices) or requires a condition, and why the Necessary is perfect in agency.

Core Idea
The Necessary Being is perfect, so any condition for emanation lies in the receiver, not the Giver.

In this passage from Sharh al-Mawaqif, al-Jurjani presents the foundational thesis for contingent beings. He explains that if a contingent's essential possibility is sufficient for receiving existence from the Necessary, it is eternal. If not, it needs a condition—but that condition cannot be on the side of the Necessary, who is perfect in agency. This principle is crucial for understanding the classical Kalam argument for the temporality of the world.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Carefully read the Arabic passage and its English translation. Notice how the author structures the two cases.
2
Identify the two cases
The passage presents two scenarios: (1) essential possibility suffices → eternal, (2) essential possibility does not suffice → needs a condition. Mark where each case is discussed.
Pay attention to the phrases 'إن كفي' and 'وإلا'.
3
Understand why the Necessary is perfect
The commentator explains that the Necessary is perfect in agency, with no deficiency. Therefore, any condition for emanation must be from the receiver, not the Giver. Reflect on this reasoning.
This contrasts with common misconceptions that God might need conditions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كلامهم في هذا المقام : ( أن الممكن إن كفي في صدوره عن الواجب تعالى إمكانه الذاتي اللازم لماهيته ( دام بدوامه ) ؛ لأن الواجب تام في فاعليته، لا قصور في فيضه، ولا بخل هناك، ولا تفاوت إلا من جهة القابل، فإذا فرض أن إمكانه الذاتي كاف في قبول الفيض، لم يتصور تخلفه عنه، فكان دائم الوجود بدوام الواجب، كالمعلول الأول . ( وإلا ) وإن لم يكف إمكانه الذاتي في الصدور ( احتاج إلى شرط) به يفيض الوجود من الواجب عليه، فإن كان ذلك الشرط قديماً (دام ) الممكن ( أيضاً ) بدوام الواجب، وشرطه القديم، فلا يتصور أن يكون الممكن الصادر من الواجب على أحد هذين الوجهين حادثاً. وإن كان ذلك الشرط ( حادثاً ) كان الممكن المتوقف عليه حادثاً بالضرورة ، لكن لما كان ذلك الشرط حادثاً ( احتاج إلى حادث (آخر)؛ إذ دلالتها وهمية فلا يرد أن الدلالة المذكورة صريحة في تلك العبارة وأن الظهور ينافي الإبهام . قوله : (أي تحقيق كلامهم لا تحقيق الإمكان الاستعدادي على ما يتبادر من قربه في الذكر، بناء على أن التحقيق المذكور مشتمل على إثبات الإمكان الاستعدادي مع إثبات أنه قائم بالمدة . قوله : ( لأن الواجب تام إلخ فلا شرط لتأثيره وفاعليته ولذا قال : إن الممكن إن كفى إلخ، ولم يقل : إن الواجب إن استجمع شرائط التأثير في الأزل إلخ. وبهذا سقط ما قيل : إن الشروط المتسلسلة شروط لفاعلية الواجب، فتكون قائمة به فلا حاجة إلى محل مختص بالحادث.
Their speech in this station: (That the contingent, if its essential possibility—necessary to its quiddity—suffices for its emanation from the Necessary, Exalted, (it remains eternal by His eternity); because the Necessary is perfect in His agency, there is no deficiency in His effusion, no miserliness there, and no disparity except from the side of the receiver. So if it is supposed that its essential possibility suffices for receiving the effusion, its being delayed from it is inconceivable, so it is everlasting in existence by the everlastingness of the Necessary, like the first effect. (Otherwise) if its essential possibility does not suffice for emanation, (it needs a condition) by which existence flows from the Necessary upon it. If that condition is eternal, the contingent (also) (remains eternal) by the eternity of the Necessary and its eternal condition, so it is inconceivable that the contingent emanating from the Necessary under either of these two modes should be originated. If that condition is (originated), then the contingent dependent upon it is necessarily originated. But since that condition is originated, (it needs another originated event); for its indication is presumptive, so it is not objected that the indicated indication is explicit in that expression and that clarity contradicts ambiguity. He said: (i.e., verification of their speech, not verification of dispositional possibility as might be understood from its proximity in mention, based on the fact that the mentioned verification includes establishing dispositional possibility along with establishing that it subsists in duration. He said: (Because the Necessary is perfect, etc.) So there is no condition for His effect and agency, and therefore he said: 'If the contingent suffices, etc.', and he did not say: 'If the Necessary assembles the conditions for effect in pre-eternity, etc.' And by this it is refuted what was said: 'Serial conditions are conditions for the agency of the Necessary, so they subsist in Him, and thus there is no need for a locus specific to the originated.'
Source pages p. 12

Commentary
This passage is the lemma and its initial commentary. The lemma presents the fundamental thesis: a contingent being, if its essential possibility (imkān dhātī) suffices for its emanation from the Necessary Being, then it is eternal like the first effect. If not, it needs a condition. The commentator explains that the condition must be from the receiver, not from the agent, because the Necessary is perfect in agency. The comment on 'the verification of their speech' clarifies that the discussion concerns essential possibility, not dispositional possibility. He then refutes the objection that serial conditions could be conditions for God's agency itself, arguing that such conditions would be intrinsic to God and thus not require a specific locus for the originated, which is false.

Key Terms
إمكان ذاتي
واجب
قديم
حادث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The condition for emanation is on God's side.
Correction: The passage clarifies that the Necessary is perfect in agency, so any condition must be on the receiver's side, not the Giver's.

Checkpoint
Why is the contingent eternal if its essential possibility suffices for emanation?
A) Because the contingent has eternal duration by itself.
B) Because the Necessary is perfect in agency and there is no deficiency in His effusion.
C) Because the contingent's quiddity is necessary.
D) Because the condition is eternal.

Key Takeaway
The perfect agency of the Necessary Being implies that any condition for contingent existence must be in the contingent itself, not in the Necessary.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a deficiency in your spiritual state, do you tend to blame external circumstances or God, rather than looking at your own capacity to receive? How does this lesson's emphasis on 'disparity only from the side of the receiver' challenge you to take responsibility?
?
This passage teaches that God's effusion is perfect and without miserliness. In what areas of your life do you still doubt God's generosity, and what does that reveal about your own inner condition as the 'receiver'?
?
If you truly internalized that any condition for receiving God's grace is on your side, what would you change starting today? Be specific—what condition can you actively remove or fulfill?

Originated Conditions and the Nature of Possibility
Explains the originated condition scenario and clarifies the nature of possibility.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why an originated condition leads to an infinite regress, and how al-Jurjani clarifies the distinction between essential and dispositional possibility.

Core Idea
An originated condition requires an endless chain, which is impossible; thus the condition must be eternal if the contingent is to exist.

Having established the two scenarios for contingent emanation, al-Jurjani now considers the case where the condition is originated. He shows that this leads to an infinite regress, which is unacceptable. He then clarifies that his discussion concerns essential possibility, not dispositional possibility, and refutes an objection that serial conditions could be conditions for God's agency itself.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on originated condition
Read the Arabic and translation carefully. Note the structure: condition is originated → contingent is originated → condition needs another condition, ad infinitum.
2
Understand the regress argument
The argument shows that if a condition is originated, it itself requires an originated condition, leading to an infinite regress. This is impossible, so the original contingent cannot be originated. Hence, the condition must be eternal.
This is a classic Kalam argument against the possibility of an infinite regress of conditions.
3
Grasp the clarification and refutation
The commentator distinguishes essential possibility (imkān dhātī) from dispositional possibility (imkān isti'dādī). He then refutes the objection that serial conditions could be conditions for God's agency, affirming that they are conditions for the receiver, not the agent.
Note the phrase 'دلالتها وهمية' meaning the indication is presumptive.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كلامهم في هذا المقام : ( أن الممكن إن كفي في صدوره عن الواجب تعالى إمكانه الذاتي اللازم لماهيته ( دام بدوامه ) ؛ لأن الواجب تام في فاعليته، لا قصور في فيضه، ولا بخل هناك، ولا تفاوت إلا من جهة القابل، فإذا فرض أن إمكانه الذاتي كاف في قبول الفيض، لم يتصور تخلفه عنه، فكان دائم الوجود بدوام الواجب، كالمعلول الأول . ( وإلا ) وإن لم يكف إمكانه الذاتي في الصدور ( احتاج إلى شرط) به يفيض الوجود من الواجب عليه، فإن كان ذلك الشرط قديماً (دام ) الممكن ( أيضاً ) بدوام الواجب، وشرطه القديم، فلا يتصور أن يكون الممكن الصادر من الواجب على أحد هذين الوجهين حادثاً. وإن كان ذلك الشرط ( حادثاً ) كان الممكن المتوقف عليه حادثاً بالضرورة ، لكن لما كان ذلك الشرط حادثاً ( احتاج إلى حادث (آخر)؛ إذ دلالتها وهمية فلا يرد أن الدلالة المذكورة صريحة في تلك العبارة وأن الظهور ينافي الإبهام . قوله : (أي تحقيق كلامهم لا تحقيق الإمكان الاستعدادي على ما يتبادر من قربه في الذكر، بناء على أن التحقيق المذكور مشتمل على إثبات الإمكان الاستعدادي مع إثبات أنه قائم بالمدة . قوله : ( لأن الواجب تام إلخ فلا شرط لتأثيره وفاعليته ولذا قال : إن الممكن إن كفى إلخ، ولم يقل : إن الواجب إن استجمع شرائط التأثير في الأزل إلخ. وبهذا سقط ما قيل : إن الشروط المتسلسلة شروط لفاعلية الواجب، فتكون قائمة به فلا حاجة إلى محل مختص بالحادث.
Their speech in this station: (That the contingent, if its essential possibility—necessary to its quiddity—suffices for its emanation from the Necessary, Exalted, (it remains eternal by His eternity); because the Necessary is perfect in His agency, there is no deficiency in His effusion, no miserliness there, and no disparity except from the side of the receiver. A) They are conditions for the agency of the Necessary.
B) They are impossible because they would require an infinite regress.
C) They are conditions for the receiver, not the agent.
D) They subsist in duration.

Key Takeaway
An originated condition requires another originated condition ad infinitum, making a first originated impossible; thus the condition must be eternal if the contingent is to exist.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God's agency requires no conditions, how does this confront your tendency to treat people, possessions, or circumstances as essential for God's help or blessing? In what area of your life are you acting as if God's power depends on something you control?
?
The argument reveals that an endless chain of causes is impossible. When you worry about the future, do you find yourself looking for a chain of human efforts or material causes rather than resting in the First Cause? How can this truth reshape your trust in divine providence today?
?
The commentator warns against confusing dispositional possibility with essential possibility. Are there desires or plans you hold as 'possible' for you that are actually outside God's decree? Will you submit to His determination even if it means giving up what you mistakenly think is possible?

The Condition Must Be Existent: Refuting the Non-Existent Condition
Argues that the condition must be existent, refuting the possibility of a non-existent condition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why a condition for an originated thing must be existent, and how the possibility of a non-existent condition leads to logical contradictions.

Core Idea
A condition cannot be non-existent because that would imply eternity or entail absurdities.

This lesson examines a key argument in kalam regarding causality: the condition for the existence of an originated thing must itself be existent. The commentator refutes the idea that a non-existent could serve as a condition by showing the logical consequences of each possible interpretation of non-existence. Understanding this argument clarifies the nature of causal conditions and avoids theological errors.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Let the argument's flow come through before you interpret.
The passage is an objection-and-answer structure.
2
Understand the division of existence
The passage states that the existent is confined to the eternal (qadim) and the originated (hadith). The condition must be one of these.
3
Examine the three ways non-existence can be considered
Non-existence can be prior, continuous, or subsequent. The passage argues that prior and continuous non-existence are eternal and thus cannot be conditions. Subsequent non-existence would imply existence as well.
This is the core of the argument.
4
Follow the objection and its refutation
The objection proposes a renewed non-existent that is neither eternal nor originated. The refutation shows that this leads to absurdities (removal of the Necessary or infinite regress). The conclusion is that non-existence after existence may be intrinsic to the essence.
This step shows how the argument handles counterarguments.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( فإن كان ذلك الشرط قديماً إلخ) يعني أن ذلك الشرط لا بد أن يكون موجوداً، والموجود منحصر في القديم والحادث، فإن كان الشرط قديماً إلخ؛ وذلك لأن المعدوم لا يجوز أن يكون شرطاً لوجود الحادث باعتبار عدمه السابق ولا باعتبار عدمه المستمر، لكونهما أزليين، فيكون باعتبار عدمه اللاحق، وذلك يستلزم كونه شرطاً باعتبار الوجود أيضاً. وبهذا سقط ما قيل : يجوز أن يكون شرطه أمراً معدوماً متجدداً فلا يكون قديماً ولا حادثاً، يوجد بعضها عقب بعض إلخ . فإن قلت عدمه بعد الوجود لا يحصل إلا بزوال علة وجوده بتلك العلة فإن كانت موجودات صرفة يستلزم زوالها زوال الواجب ؛ لاستناد الموجودات كلها إليه. وإن كانت مركبة من الموجودات والمعدومات وكان زوالها بزوال المعدومات يلزم وجود الأمور الغير المتناهية المترتبة المجتمعة : قلت : يجوز أن يكون عدمه بعد الوجود مقتضى ذاته، فلا يحتاج إلى عدم علة وجوده .
He said: (If that condition is eternal, etc.) meaning that that condition must be existent, and the existent is confined to the eternal and the originated. If the condition is eternal, etc.; and that is because the non-existent cannot be a condition for the existence of the originated in respect of its prior non-existence nor in respect of its continuous non-existence, because both are eternal, so it would be in respect of its subsequent non-existence, and that entails its being a condition in respect of existence as well. And by this it is refuted what was said: 'It is permissible that its condition be a renewed non-existent, so it is neither eternal nor originated, some occurring after others, etc.' For if you say: Its non-existence after existence only occurs by the removal of the cause of its existence by that cause; if they are pure existents, their removal entails the removal of the Necessary, because all existents are dependent upon Him. And if they are composed of existents and non-existents, and their removal is by the removal of the non-existents, it necessitates the existence of infinite, ordered, simultaneous things. I say: It is permissible that its non-existence after existence is a requirement of its essence, so it does not need the removal of the cause of its existence.
Source pages p. 12

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer. The commentator explains that if the condition is eternal, it must be existent. He argues that non-existence cannot be a condition for the existence of an originated thing, whether considered as prior non-existence or continuous non-existence, because both are eternal. The only possibility is subsequent non-existence, but that would require existence as well. He then refutes the objection that the condition could be a renewed non-existent, which is neither eternal nor originated. He shows that this leads to absurdities: if the removal of the cause is by pure existents, it implies the removal of the Necessary; if by a mix, it leads to an infinite regress of simultaneous things. He concludes that non-existence after existence can be intrinsic to the essence itself.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think a non-existent can serve as a condition for an originated being.
Correction: The argument shows that non-existence considered in any aspect leads to contradictions: prior/continuous non-existence is eternal, subsequent non-existence implies existence, and the idea of a renewed non-existent leads to absurdities.

Checkpoint
Why cannot a non-existent be a condition for an originated being?
A) Because non-existence is not a real entity.
B) Because considering prior or continuous non-existence would make the condition eternal, which is inconsistent.
C) Because non-existence has no causal power.
D) Because the necessary being must be the condition.

Key Takeaway
The condition for an originated thing must be existent; a non-existent condition leads to logical contradictions, as shown by the argument.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

According to this lesson, if that condition is non-existent, it cannot be a true condition. What does this reveal about your hesitation? What step can you take today to act without waiting for a non-existent condition?
?
The passage concludes that non-existence after existence may be intrinsic to the essence itself, without needing removal of a cause. Is there something in your character or habits that you consider 'intrinsically' removed from good? How might this understanding break the cycle of blame and shift your reliance solely on Allah's power to create change?

The Originated Condition Leads to an Infinite Regress
Rebuts the objection that the originated condition could be non-existent, showing it leads to infinite regress.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why an originated condition for an originated being leads to an infinite regress, and why this regress is impossible according to kalam reasoning.

Core Idea
If the condition for an originated being is itself originated, an endless chain results — a logical impossibility.

In this passage, the commentator addresses an objection: could the condition for an originated being be a non-existent or a renewed non-existent? He shows that such proposals fail — either the non-existent is eternal and thus cannot condition an originated, or it is originated and would itself require a condition, leading to an infinite regress. This argument establishes that the condition must be eternal.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
Read the objector's suggestion: the condition for an originated being could be a non-existent (ʿadam) or a renewed non-existent. Notice the attempt to avoid an infinite chain.
2
Follow the rebuttal
The commentator rejects the non-existent condition: prior non-existence is eternal, so it cannot condition the originated; subsequent non-existence entails existence, bringing back the original problem.
3
Grasp the regress argument
If the condition is itself originated, it must have its own condition, leading to an infinite chain of originated events. This is impossible, so the condition must be eternal.
This is the core of the lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( احتاج إلى حادث آخر فيه بحث لم لا يجوز أن لا يكون الشرط الحادث أمراً عدمياً؟ وإن نوقش في إطلاق الحادث على العدمي يقول : لم لا يجوز أن يكون شرط الحادث أمراً عدمياً متجدداً؟ وقد سبق أن التجدد لا يستلزم الوجود لا يقال العدم السابق أزلي، فلا يكون شرطاً للحادث، وشرطية العدم اللاحق يستلزم شرطية الوجود؛ لتوقفه عليه فيعود المحذور؛ لأنا لو لم يتوقف ذلك الشرط على شرط آخر أصلاً، أو كان شرطه قديماً لم يكن هو حادثاً، وذلك الشرط الآخر الحادث محتاج أيضاً إلى حادث ثالث قبله، (وهلم جرا. فيتوقف كل حادث على حادث إلى مالا نهاية له.
He said: (It needs another originated event) — there is a discussion: Why is it not permissible that the originated condition be a non-existent thing? And if there is objection to applying 'originated' to the non-existent, he says: Why is it not permissible that the condition of the originated be a renewed non-existent? And it has preceded that renewal does not entail existence. It is not said: Prior non-existence is eternal, so it cannot be a condition for the originated, and the conditionality of subsequent non-existence entails conditionality of existence because it depends on it, so the problem returns; for if that condition did not depend on another condition at all, or its condition was eternal, it would not be originated, and that other originated condition also needs a third originated before it, and so on. So every originated depends on an originated to infinity.
Source pages p. 12

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer. The objector suggests that the originated condition could be a non-existent (ʿadamī) thing, or a renewed non-existent. The commentator rebuts by pointing out that renewal does not imply existence, and that prior non-existence is eternal, so it cannot condition an originated. If subsequent non-existence is considered, it would entail existence. He then presents the core argument: if the condition is originated, it itself must have a condition, leading to an infinite regress of originated events. Thus, the conclusion is that an originated condition leads to an infinite chain, which is impossible.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: A non-existent can serve as a condition for an originated being without causing any logical problem.
Correction: The commentator shows that a non-existent condition either is eternal (prior non-existence) and thus cannot condition an originated, or it is originated and leads to an infinite regress. Therefore, a non-existent cannot be a valid condition.

Checkpoint
What is the consequence of assuming the condition for an originated being is itself originated?
A) It becomes eternal.
B) It requires an infinite chain of conditions.
C) It becomes non-existent.
D) It is impossible because the condition must be eternal.

Key Takeaway
The condition for an originated being must be eternal; otherwise, an infinite regress of originated conditions results.

?
The objection tried to escape the need for an eternal condition by appealing to non-existence. Are there areas in your life where you try to avoid accountability by denying the need for an eternal foundation? What would it mean to honestly face that need today?

The Core Proof Against Simultaneous Infinite Series
Presents the main proof against simultaneous infinite series using the set-condition contradiction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the core argument proving the impossibility of an infinite series of simultaneous originated events, specifically the contradiction that the set of events would require a condition that is both inside and outside itself.

Core Idea
A simultaneous infinite series forces a condition to be both inside and outside its own set — an impossible contradiction.

Ibn al-Ḥājib and later commentators such as al-Ījī and al-Jurjānī establish that any series of originated events occurring simultaneously cannot be infinite. The proof hinges on the nature of the whole set: since the set itself is originated, it requires an originated condition, leading to a logical contradiction. This lesson presents that foundational argument from the text.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once and follow the translation. Notice the logical structure: the author first states the two possibilities for ordered events, then focuses on the simultaneous case.
Pay attention to the terms 'مجموع' (set) and 'شرط' (condition).
2
Identify the key components of the argument
Find the statements: the set of simultaneous events is originated, it requires a condition, that condition is one of the events (inside), but as a condition it must be prior (outside).
Look for the words 'داخلاً' (inside) and 'خارجاً' (outside).
3
Understand the contradiction
Reflect on why a condition cannot be both inside and outside the same set. The condition's priority over the set requires it to be outside, yet as an event it is part of the set.
This contradiction shows the impossibility of simultaneous infinite series.
4
Connect to the broader proof
Realize that this contradiction invalidates the simultaneous case, leaving the non-simultaneous (successive) possibility. The next lessons will address objections and further nuances.
This lesson covers only the first part of the passage; subsequent lessons handle responses to objections.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فهي أي تلك الحوادث المترتبة إما موجودة معا وهو باطل؛ لما سيأتي من برهان التطبيق الدال على استحالة التسلسل في الأمور المترتبة طبعاً، أو وضعاً مع كونها موجودة معاً، (ولأن ذاك المجموع المركب من تلك الحوادث الموجودة على الاجتماع ( يحتاج ) ؛ لكونه حادثاً إلى شرط آخر حادث أيضاً، لما عرفت ( فيكون ذلك الشرط الآخر الحادث ( داخلاً) في المجموع؛ لأنه من جملة الحوادث المترتبة، وقد أخذ مجموعها بحيث لا يشذ عنه شيء، وخارجاً عن ذلك المجموع أيضاً؛ لكونه شرطاً له سابقاً

قوله: (ولأن ذلك المجموع يعني إذا كانت تلك الحوادث موجودة معاً، كان هناك مجموع في الخارج حادث، لوجوب حدوث الكل عند حدوث الجزء، موصوف بحدوث مغاير لحدوث الجزء؛ لكونه معللاً به فاندفع ما قيل : إنه ليس في الخارج إلا الآحاد المستند بعضها إلى بعض ولا مجموع هاهنا، لأن مغايرة الكل المجموعي لكل واحد بديهي، وكذا ما قيل : إن هذا الدليل جار في صورة التعاقب أيضاً، أو نقول : تلك الحوادث المتعاقبة حادثة، فيحتاج إلى شرط حادث داخل فيها وخارج عنها؛ إذ ليس في الخارج في صورة التعاقب في شيء من الأزمنة إلا حادث واحد مشروط بحادث سابق عليه، ومجموعها ممتنع الوجود في الخارج فكيف يحتاج إلى شرط حادث .

قوله : ( لأنه من جملة الحوادث المترتبة وبهذا اندفع ما توهم من أنه يجوز أن يكون ذلك الشرط خارجاً من مجموع تلك الحوادث مشروطاً بحادث آخر، فإن اعتبر هذا المجموع يكون مشروطاً بحادث آخر خارج عنه وهلم جراً، فلا يلزم دخول ذلك الشرط في شيء من المجموعات . ووجه الدفع ظاهر لأنا أخذنا جميع الشروط التي يتوقف عليها وجود الحادث.

قوله : ( وخارجاً عن ذلك المجموع فيه بحث، لأن اللازم مما ذكر أن يكون كل حادث موقوفاً وجوده على حادث آخر كيلا يلزم قدمه بسبب استناده إلى الواجب القديم، وأما أن ذلك الحادث الموقوف عليه يجب أن يكون خارجاً عنه فكلاً، فيجوز أن يكون حدوث المجموع بواسطة حدوث جزأيه وهو ما عدا الشرط الأخير الذي يتصل بوجوده وجود الحادث المفروض

نقول : فرق بين العدمي والعدم كما مر في بحث التعين فإن قلت ذلك الأمر العدمي يستدعي أيضاً محلاً، وإلا تساوت النسبة، كما سيأتي . قلت : لا نسلم اقتضاء المحل الموجود فإن قلت ء أن الشرط مقرب ولا قرب في المعدوم المحض قلت : سيجيء أيضاً ما في حديث سيجيء القرب .
So they—i.e., those ordered originated events—are either existent simultaneously, and that is invalid because of what will come of the proof of application (burhān al-taṭbīq) indicating the impossibility of series in things ordered naturally or positionally while being simultaneously existent, (and because that composite set composed of those events existing together (needs), because it is originated, another originated condition as well, as you have known, (so that other originated condition would be (inside) the set, because it is among the ordered originated events, and its set has been taken such that nothing escapes it, and also outside that set, because it is a condition for it prior.

He said: (And because that set) means if those events existed together, there would be an external originated set, due to the necessary origination of the whole when a part originates, described by an origination different from the origination of the part, because it is caused by it. So it is refuted what was said: 'There is nothing external but individuals depending on each other, and no set here,' because the difference of the whole set from each individual is self-evident. And likewise what was said: 'This argument also applies to the case of succession,' or we say: Those successive events are originated, so they need an originated condition inside them and outside them; for in the case of succession, at no time is there more than one originated event conditioned by a preceding one, and their set is impossible in external existence, so how does it need an originated condition?

He said: (Because it is among the ordered originated events) and by this is refuted the misconception that it is permissible for that condition to be outside the set of those events, conditioned by another originated event; for if this set is considered, it is conditioned by another originated event outside it, and so on, so the inclusion of that condition in any of the sets is not necessary. And the refutation is clear because we took all the conditions upon which the existence of the originated depends.

He said: (And outside that set) — there is discussion: Because the necessary from what was mentioned is that every originated is dependent for its existence on another originated, so that its eternity due to its dependence on the eternal Necessary does not follow. But as for that originated upon which it depends being necessarily outside it, not at all. It is permissible that the origination of the set be through the origination of its two parts, which is what is other than the last condition by whose existence the existence of the supposed originated connects.

We say: There is a difference between the non-existent thing (al-ʿadamī) and non-existence (al-ʿadam), as passed in the discussion of determination. For if you say: That non-existent thing also requires a locus, otherwise the relation would be equal, as will come. I say: We do not accept that it necessitates an existent locus. For if you say: The condition is a means of approximation, and there is no approximation in pure non-existence. I say: There will also come what is in the discussion of proximity.
Source pages p. 13

Commentary
This passage presents the proof that an infinite series of simultaneous originated events is impossible. The commentator first states that the ordered events are either simultaneous (invalid due to the proof of application) or not. For simultaneous existence, the set itself would be originated and require a condition, which would both be inside the set (as one of the events) and outside it (as its condition), a contradiction. He then defends this argument against objection: (1) That there is no external set—he asserts the set's existence is self-evident. (2) That the argument applies to succession—he responds that in succession only one event exists at a time, so no set problem. (3) That the condition could be outside the set, avoiding interior contradiction—he responds that all conditions are included. Finally, he discusses the difference between a non-existent thing and non-existence, and the need for a locus, deferring to later discussions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that an infinite series can exist simultaneously if each event has its own cause, without needing an overall condition for the entire set.
Correction: The passage shows that the set itself is an originated entity requiring a condition, regardless of whether individual events have their own causes.

Checkpoint
What contradiction arises if an infinite series of originated events exists simultaneously?
A) The set would be both eternal and originated.
B) The set would need a condition that is both inside and outside it.
C) The events would have no cause.
D) The events cannot be ordered.

Key Takeaway
An infinite series of simultaneous originated events is impossible because the set of events would require a condition that is both inside and outside it, which is a contradiction.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Does your heart truly rest on the belief that every condition ultimately traces back to an Unconditioned? Or do you quietly assume that some things can go on forever without a sufficient reason? Answer honestly: where in your life do you act as if the chain of conditions could be infinite, ignoring the need for a First Cause?
?
This proof shows that a condition cannot be both inside and outside the set of all events. Reflect: Are there conditions in your own life—your habits, your beliefs, your dependencies—that you try to keep both ‘inside’ (as part of your identity) and ‘outside’ (as something you think you could drop)? What contradiction might that be causing in your relationship with your Creator?
?
If every originated thing needs a condition outside itself, what does that mean for you, an originated being? Can you honestly say you have acknowledged the Condition that gave you existence, or do you live as if your being is self-sufficient? Let this proof press on your soul: you are not the set that contains its own condition. You are in need. Will you turn to the Unconditioned today?

Defending Against Objections: No External Set and Succession
Responds to two objections: no real set and applicability to succession.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the commentator refutes two objections: (1) that there is no real external set, and (2) that the argument also applies to successive events.

Core Idea
The set of simultaneous events is real and self-evident, and the proof does not apply to successive events because no simultaneous set exists there.

After presenting the core proof against simultaneous infinite series, the commentator addresses two potential objections. The first objection denies that the set of simultaneous events has real existence, claiming only individual events exist. The second objection claims that the same argument would make successive series impossible. This lesson explains how the commentator refutes both misgivings using clear reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and translation, focusing on the two objections and responses.
Look for the phrases 'ما قيل' (what was said) indicating objections.
2
Understand the first objection
Identify the claim that there is no external set beyond individual events. The commentator asserts the set's existence is self-evident.
Key phrase: 'أنه ليس في الخارج إلا الآحاد' (there is nothing external but individuals).
3
Understand the second objection
Recognize the claim that the same argument applies to successive events. The commentator responds that in succession, only one event exists at a time, so there is no simultaneous set requiring a condition.
Note the distinction between simultaneous and successive existence.
4
Reflect on the strength of the refutations
Consider why these responses are effective: the set's reality is obvious, and the absence of a simultaneous set in succession avoids the contradiction.
This strengthens the original proof against simultaneous series.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فهي أي تلك الحوادث المترتبة إما موجودة معا وهو باطل؛ لما سيأتي من برهان التطبيق الدال على استحالة التسلسل في الأمور المترتبة طبعاً، أو وضعاً مع كونها موجودة معاً، (ولأن ذاك المجموع المركب من تلك الحوادث الموجودة على الاجتماع ( يحتاج ) ؛ لكونه حادثاً إلى شرط آخر حادث أيضاً، لما عرفت ( فيكون ذلك الشرط الآخر الحادث ( داخلاً) في المجموع؛ لأنه من جملة الحوادث المترتبة، وقد أخذ مجموعها بحيث لا يشذ عنه شيء، وخارجاً عن ذلك المجموع أيضاً؛ لكونه شرطاً له سابقاً

قوله: (ولأن ذلك المجموع يعني إذا كانت تلك الحوادث موجودة معاً، كان هناك مجموع في الخارج حادث، لوجوب حدوث الكل عند حدوث الجزء، موصوف بحدوث مغاير لحدوث الجزء؛ لكونه معللاً به فاندفع ما قيل : إنه ليس في الخارج إلا الآحاد المستند بعضها إلى بعض ولا مجموع هاهنا، لأن مغايرة الكل المجموعي لكل واحد بديهي، وكذا ما قيل : إن هذا الدليل جار في صورة التعاقب أيضاً، أو نقول : تلك الحوادث المتعاقبة حادثة، فيحتاج إلى شرط حادث داخل فيها وخارج عنها؛ إذ ليس في الخارج في صورة التعاقب في شيء من الأزمنة إلا حادث واحد مشروط بحادث سابق عليه، ومجموعها ممتنع الوجود في الخارج فكيف يحتاج إلى شرط حادث .

قوله : ( لأنه من جملة الحوادث المترتبة وبهذا اندفع ما توهم من أنه يجوز أن يكون ذلك الشرط خارجاً من مجموع تلك الحوادث مشروطاً بحادث آخر، فإن اعتبر هذا المجموع يكون مشروطاً بحادث آخر خارج عنه وهلم جراً، فلا يلزم دخول ذلك الشرط في شيء من المجموعات . ووجه الدفع ظاهر لأنا أخذنا جميع الشروط التي يتوقف عليها وجود الحادث.

قوله : ( وخارجاً عن ذلك المجموع فيه بحث، لأن اللازم مما ذكر أن يكون كل حادث موقوفاً وجوده على حادث آخر كيلا يلزم قدمه بسبب استناده إلى الواجب القديم، وأما أن ذلك الحادث الموقوف عليه يجب أن يكون خارجاً عنه فكلاً، فيجوز أن يكون حدوث المجموع بواسطة حدوث جزأيه وهو ما عدا الشرط الأخير الذي يتصل بوجوده وجود الحادث المفروض

نقول : فرق بين العدمي والعدم كما مر في بحث التعين فإن قلت ذلك الأمر العدمي يستدعي أيضاً محلاً، وإلا تساوت النسبة، كما سيأتي . قلت : لا نسلم اقتضاء المحل الموجود فإن قلت ء أن الشرط مقرب ولا قرب في المعدوم المحض قلت : سيجيء أيضاً ما في حديث سيجيء القرب .
So they—i.e., those ordered originated events—are either existent simultaneously, and that is invalid because of what will come of the proof of application (burhān al-taṭbīq) indicating the impossibility of series in things ordered naturally or positionally while being simultaneously existent, (and because that composite set composed of those events existing together (needs), because it is originated, another originated condition as well, as you have known, (so that other originated condition would be (inside) the set, because it is among the ordered originated events, and its set has been taken such that nothing escapes it, and also outside that set, because it is a condition for it prior.

He said: (And because that set) means if those events existed together, there would be an external originated set, due to the necessary origination of the whole when a part originates, described by an origination different from the origination of the part, because it is caused by it. So it is refuted what was said: 'There is nothing external but individuals depending on each other, and no set here,' because the difference of the whole set from each individual is self-evident. And likewise what was said: 'This argument also applies to the case of succession,' or we say: Those successive events are originated, so they need an originated condition inside them and outside them; for in the case of succession, at no time is there more than one originated event conditioned by a preceding one, and their set is impossible in external existence, so how does it need an originated condition?

He said: (Because it is among the ordered originated events) and by this is refuted the misconception that it is permissible for that condition to be outside the set of those events, conditioned by another originated event; for if this set is considered, it is conditioned by another originated event outside it, and so on, so the inclusion of that condition in any of the sets is not necessary. And the refutation is clear because we took all the conditions upon which the existence of the originated depends.

He said: (And outside that set) — there is discussion: Because the necessary from what was mentioned is that every originated is dependent for its existence on another originated, so that its eternity due to its dependence on the eternal Necessary does not follow. But as for that originated upon which it depends being necessarily outside it, not at all. It is permissible that the origination of the set be through the origination of its two parts, which is what is other than the last condition by whose existence the existence of the supposed originated connects.

We say: There is a difference between the non-existent thing (al-ʿadamī) and non-existence (al-ʿadam), as passed in the discussion of determination. For if you say: That non-existent thing also requires a locus, otherwise the relation would be equal, as will come. I say: We do not accept that it necessitates an existent locus. For if you say: The condition is a means of approximation, and there is no approximation in pure non-existence. I say: There will also come what is in the discussion of proximity.
Source pages p. 13

Commentary
This passage presents the proof that an infinite series of simultaneous originated events is impossible. The commentator first states that the ordered events are either simultaneous (invalid due to the proof of application) or not. For simultaneous existence, the set itself would be originated and require a condition, which would both be inside the set (as one of the events) and outside it (as its condition), a contradiction. He then defends this argument against objection: (1) That there is no external set—he asserts the set's existence is self-evident. (2) That the argument applies to succession—he responds that in succession only one event exists at a time, so no set problem. (3) That the condition could be outside the set, avoiding interior contradiction—he responds that all conditions are included. Finally, he discusses the difference between a non-existent thing and non-existence, and the need for a locus, deferring to later discussions.

Key Terms

حادث
شرط
تعاقب
برهان التطبيق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the commentator's response to the objection that there is no real set of simultaneous events?
A) He accepts the objection and modifies the proof.
B) He argues that the set's existence is self-evident.
C) He says the set is only conceptual.
D) He changes the subject.

Key Takeaway
The set of simultaneous events is real and self-evident, and the proof does not apply to successive events because no simultaneous set exists in succession.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter a logical objection to a belief you hold, do you rush to defend it broadly, or do you first carefully examine the objection's assumptions as the commentator does here? How can you apply this lesson's methodology of precise refutation in your own theological reflections?
?
The passage asserts that the distinction between the whole and its parts is self-evident. Are there truths in your faith that you accept as self-evident, even if you cannot fully explain them? How does that intellectual humility affect your relationship with Allah?
?
Consider a time you generalized a rule without checking its specific conditions. How might this lesson's distinction between simultaneous and successive series change the way you approach arguments in your own life, whether in religious or everyday matters?

Causality and Created Things

Further Objections and the Nuance of the Condition
Addresses the objection that condition could be outside the set and discusses non-existent vs. non-existence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the objection that the condition could be outside the set, the commentator's response, and the distinction between non-existent thing and non-existence.

Core Idea
Even if the condition is outside the set, it still must be included in the all-encompassing set, and non-existence differs from a non-existent thing.

The previous lesson addressed two objections; here the commentator tackles a more subtle objection: could the condition for the set be outside the set, avoiding the contradiction? He responds that the set already includes all conditions, so any such condition would still be inside. The passage also introduces an important distinction between a non-existent thing (al-ʿadamī) and absolute non-existence (al-ʿadam), which will be treated in later discussions.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage covering paragraphs 3, 4, and 5, and the corresponding translation.
Notice the phrase 'فيه بحث' indicating a point of discussion.
2
Understand the third objection
Some suggest the condition for the set could be outside the set, escaping the contradiction. The commentator refutes by noting that all conditions are included in the set of all events.
Key phrase: 'أخذنا جميع الشروط' (we took all conditions).
3
Grasp the discussion on being 'outside'
The commentator then examines the idea that the condition being outside might be necessary, but he argues it is not required. He allows for the set's origination through partial causes.
This part is more nuanced and shows the flexibility of the argument.
4
Understand the distinction between non-existent thing and non-existence
The passage touches on a subtle point: a non-existent thing (like a condition) is not the same as non-existence. This distinction is important for further debates but is deferred.
Look for 'فرق بين العدمي والعدم' (difference between the non-existent thing and non-existence).
